Criterion for Horseman or Foot Soldier: The Moment of Crossing
Detailed ruling on spoils share determination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the status of a fighter (horseman or foot soldier) for spoils shares is determined at the moment of crossing into enemy territory, and distinguish cases where this rule is modified.

Core Idea
The crossing moment decides the share—later changes in mount do not affect entitlement.

In the distribution of spoils (ghanima), the Hanafi school distinguishes between horsemen (faris) who receive a larger share and foot soldiers (rajil) who receive a smaller share. But when exactly is a fighter's status fixed? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes that the decisive moment is the crossing (mujawaza) into enemy territory. The reasoning is that crossing itself is an act of combat, and it is impractical to gauge actual fighting later. This lesson explores the rule and its many applications.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The text begins: 'والعبرة للفارس والراجل عند المجاوزة'. So the criterion is the time of crossing.
This is the default ruling.
2
Identify the reasoning (ta'lil)
Because crossing itself is a form of fighting (terror), and actual fighting is hard to ascertain.
The author provides two reasons: crossing causes fear, and detailed observation of battle is impractical.
3
Analyze the default scenarios
If one enters as horseman, even if horse dies later, he gets horseman share; if enters on foot, even if later acquires horse, he gets foot soldier share.
Death of horse or later acquisition does not change the status.
4
Examine the exceptions based on actions contrary to intent
Selling, mortgaging, leasing, giving away the horse before or during battle indicates lack of intent to fight as horseman, so no horseman share.
These actions show the fighter did not intend to fight as a horseman from the start.
5
Consider the disputed cases (intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf)
Cases of borrowed/usurped horse recovered by owner, or horse lost then found. There are two narrations; the preferred view is to give horseman share if terror was achieved and fault was not the fighter's.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq leans towards the horseman's share in such cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والعبرة للفارس والراجل عند المجاوزة) لأن المجاوزة نفسها قتال لأنهم يلحقون الخوف بها والحالة بعدها حالة الدوام ولا معتبر بها، ولأن الوقوف على حقيقة القتال متعسر، وكذا على شهود الوقعة لأنه حالة التقاء الصفين فتقام المجاوزة مقامه إذ هو السبب المفضي إليه ظاهراً إذا كان على قصد القتال فيعتبر حال الشخص حالة المجاوزة فارساً أو راجلاً، فلو دخل دار الحرب فارساً فنفق فرسه استحق سهم الفرسان، ولو كان بقتل رجل وأخذ القيمة منه فإذا بقي فرسه وقاتل راجلاً لضيق المكان يستحقه بالطريق الأولى، وإن دخلها راجلاً فاشترى فرساً استحق سهم راجل وهذا إذا هلك فرسه فإن دخلها فارساً ثم باعه أو رهنه أو أجره أو وهبه فإنه لا يستحق سهم الفارس في ظاهر الرواية لأن الإقدام على هذه التصرفات يدل على أنه لم يكن من قصده بالمجاوزة القتال فارساً، وكذا إذا باعه حال القتال على الأصح لدلالته على غرض التجارة إلا إذا باعه مكرهاً كما في التتارخانية بخلاف ما إذا باعه بعد انقضاء الحرب فإنه يستحق سهم الفارس. وفي الخلاصة ولو أعاره ففيه روايتان، وأما إذا دخل على فرس مغصوب أو مستعار أو مستأجر ثم استرده المالك فقاتل راجلاً ففيه روايتان ولم أر ترجيحاً، وينبغي ترجيح استحقاق سهم الفارس الحصول الإرهاب ولا صنع له في الاسترداد فصار كالهلاك بخلاف البيع وقد كتبته قبل مراجعة ما في فتح القدير ثم رأيته قال بعد ذكر الروايتين : ومقتضى كونه جاوز بفرس لقصد القتال عليه ترجيح الاستحقاق إلا أن يزاد في أجزاء السبب بفرس مملوك وهو ممنوع فإنه لو لم يسترد المعير وغيره حتى قاتل عليه كان فارساً .اهـ. قالوا ويشترط أن يكون الفرس صالحاً للقتال بأن يكون صحيحاً كبيراً حتى لو دخل بمهر أو مريض لا يستحق سهم الفرسان لأنه لا يقصد به القتال . التتارخانية : لو زال المرض وصار بحال يقاتل عليه قبل الغنيمة فالقياس أن لا يسهم له . وفي الاستحسان يسهم له بخلاف ما إذا طال المكث في دار الحرب حتى بلغ المهر وصار صالحاً للركوب فقاتل عليه لا يستحق سهم الفرسان اهـ. وكان الفرق هو أن الإرهاب حاصل بالكبير المريض في الجملة بخلافه في المهر وفيها : لو غصب فرسه منه قبل الدخول فدخل راجلاً ثم استرده فيها فله سهم الفارس، وكذا لو ركب رجل عليه ودخل دار الحرب، وكذا لو نفر الفرس فأتبعه ودخل راجلاً، وكذا إذا ضل منه فدخل راجلاً ثم وجده فيها فإن صاحبه لا يحرم سهم الفرس ولو وهبها ودخل راجلاً ودخل الموهوب له فارساً ثم رجع فيها استحق الموهوب له في الغنيمة سهم الفارس فيما أصابه قبل الرجوع وسهم الراجل فيما والراجع راجل مطلقاً فاسداً . كالبائع في دار الإسلام إذا استرده في دار الحرب للفساد، وكالمستحق للفرس في دار الحرب وكالراهن إذا أفتكها فيها. ولو باعها ثم وهب له أخرى وسلمت كان فارساً، ولو استردها المؤجر أو المعير فملك غيرها بشراء أو هبة فالثانية تقوم مقام الأولى، ولو كان الأول بإجارة والثاني كذلك أو بعارية والثاني كذلك فالثاني يقوم مقام الأول، ولو كان الأول بإجارة والثاني عارية فإنه لا يقوم مقامه، ولو اشتراها في دار الإسلام وتقابضا في دار الحرب فهما راجلان ولو نقده قبل الدخول وقبضها بعده فالمشتري فارس والفرس المشترك بين رجلين يقاتل هذا مرة وهذا أخرى لا له إلا إذا أجر أحدهما نصيبه من شريكه قبل الدخول فالسهم للمستأجر اهـ.
His statement: (And the consideration is for the horseman and the foot soldier at the time of crossing) because the crossing itself is fighting, as they cause fear by it, and the state after it is a state of continuity, and it is not considered. And because ascertaining the reality of fighting is difficult, likewise witnessing the battle, because it is the meeting of the two ranks, so crossing is set in its place as it is the apparent cause leading to it, if it is with the intention of fighting. So the person's state at the time of crossing is considered, whether horseman or foot soldier. So if he entered the Abode of War as a horseman and his horse died, he deserves the horseman's share. And if he killed a man and took the price from him, and his horse remained and he fought on foot due to narrowness of place, he deserves it a fortiori. And if he entered it as a foot soldier and then bought a horse, he deserves the foot soldier's share. And this is if his horse died. But if he entered as a horseman and then sold it, mortgaged it, leased it, or gave it away, then he does not deserve the horseman's share in the apparent narration, because undertaking these actions indicates that his intention in crossing was not to fight as a horseman. Likewise if he sold it during battle, according to the most correct view, because it indicates a commercial purpose, unless he was forced to sell it, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. Contrary to if he sold it after the war ended, then he deserves the horseman's share. And in al-Khulasa: if he lent it, there are two narrations. As for if he entered on a usurped, borrowed, or leased horse, and then the owner took it back, and he fought on foot: there are two narrations, and I have not seen a preponderance. But it is proper to prefer entitlement to the horseman's share because terror is achieved, and he had no hand in the recovery, so it becomes like death, contrary to sale. And I wrote this before reviewing what is in Fath al-Qadir; then I saw it said after mentioning the two narrations: 'The requirement of his having crossed with a horse intending to fight on it preponderates entitlement, unless an additional condition is imposed of a horse owned, which is prohibited. For if the lender or other had not recovered it until he fought on it, he would be a horseman.' They said: It is a condition that the horse be fit for fighting, being healthy and mature. So if he entered with a foal or a sick horse, he does not deserve the horseman's share, because he does not intend fighting with it. Al-Tatarkhaniyya: If the sickness ceased and it became in a state that one can fight on it before the spoils, by qiyas he does not get a share, but by istihsan he does, contrary to if the foal stayed in Dar al-Harb until it grew and became fit for riding, then he fought on it: he does not deserve the horseman's share. The difference is that terror is achieved by a mature sick horse in some measure, contrary to a foal. And in it: If his horse was usurped from him before entry, and he entered on foot, then recovered it there, he has the horseman's share. Likewise if a man rode on it and entered Dar al-Harb. Likewise if the horse bolted and he followed it and entered on foot. Likewise if it was lost and he entered on foot and then found it there—its owner is not deprived of the horse's share. And if he gave it away, entered on foot, and the donee entered as horseman, then it reverted to him: the donee is entitled to the horseman's share in the spoils for what was obtained before reversion, and the foot soldier's share afterwards. And the one who reverts is a foot soldier absolutely. [This is] like the seller in Dar al-Islam who takes it back in Dar al-Harb due to invalidity, and like the person entitled to the horse in Dar al-Harb, and like the pledgor when he redeems it there. And if he sold it, then another horse was given to him as a gift and it arrived, he is a horseman. And if the lessor or lender recovered it, and then he owned another by purchase or gift, the second takes the place of the first. If the first was by lease and the second likewise, or by loan and the second likewise, the second takes the place of the first. If the first was by lease and the second by loan, it does not take its place. And if he bought it in Dar al-Islam and they took possession in Dar al-Harb, both are foot soldiers. If he paid the price before entry and took possession after it, the buyer is a horseman. And the horse jointly owned by two men: each fights on it sometimes; no share for them, except if one of them leases his share to his partner before entry, then the share goes to the lessee.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This is a detailed ruling on how to determine whether a fighter qualifies as a horseman (faris) or foot soldier (rajil) for the purpose of spoils shares. The rule is: the decisive moment is the time of crossing the border into enemy territory (mujawaza). The reason is that crossing itself is an act of combat, as it instills fear in the enemy; and it is difficult to ascertain actual fighting later. So if one crosses as a horseman, he gets the horseman's share even if his horse later dies; if he crosses on foot, he gets the foot soldier's share even if he later acquires a horse. However, if he sells, mortgages, leases, or gives away his horse before crossing, it shows his intention was not to fight as a horseman, so he gets no horseman's share. The text then discusses numerous scenarios: death of the horse, forced sale, borrowed or usurped horses, recovery by owner, sickness or immaturity of the horse, joint ownership, etc. In cases of borrowed or usurped horses where the owner recovers it, there are two narrations (riwayatan), but the author inclines towards giving the horseman's share because terror was achieved and the fighter was not at fault. The condition is also stated that the horse must be fit for fighting—healthy and mature. A sick horse that recovers before the spoils may get a share by istihsan, but a foal that grows up in Dar al-Harb does not. The text ends with various scenarios involving purchases, gifts, leases, and joint ownership, all applying the principle that the status at crossing determines the share, with exceptions based on intention and ownership.

Key Terms
المجاوزة (al-mujawaza): The act of crossing the border into enemy territory (Dar al-Harb).
الرضخ (al-radhakh): A small grant given to those not entitled to a full share (sahm), such as women, children, slaves, and dhimmis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following actions would cause a fighter who crossed as a horseman to lose his horseman's share in the apparent narration?
A) His horse dies after crossing
B) He leases his horse before crossing
C) He enters on a sick horse that later recovers
D) His horse is usurped before crossing

Key Takeaway
The moment of crossing (mujawaza) is the sole determinant for a fighter's share in spoils; later changes in mount or ownership do not alter the initial classification.

Radhakh for Women, Children, Slaves, and Dhimmis
Ruling that these groups receive a small grant (radhakh) rather than a full share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of radhakh for the four categories, explain the Prophetic dalil, and distinguish radhakh from a full share (sahm).

Core Idea
Women, children, slaves, and dhimmis get radhakh, not a share, because jihad is worship and they are not full combatants.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the distinction between a full share (sahm) and a discretionary grant (radhakh) in spoils of war. While combatants are entitled to fixed shares, certain individuals — women, children, slaves, and dhimmis — receive only a small grant at the leader's discretion. The ruling is rooted in the Prophet's consistent practice and the legal principle that jihad is an act of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Categories
List the four groups mentioned: slave (mamluk), woman, child (sabi), and dhimmi. Note that these are non-combatant or partially capable participants.
The dhimmi is a non-Muslim citizen; their exclusion is based on jihad being an act of worship.
2
Understand the Ruling: Radhakh vs. Sahm
Radhakh is a small, discretionary grant; sahm is a fixed, wajib share. The text states these groups receive radhakh, not sahm.
Radhakh is not a fixed amount; it is given at the leader's discretion.
3
Trace the Dalil: Prophet's Practice
The Prophet (ﷺ) did not give shares to women, children, and slaves but gave them radhakh. Also, when he sought Jewish allies, he did not give them shares from spoils.
The hadith is reported in sunan collections; it establishes the general rule.
4
Understand the Ratio Legis (Illah)
Jihad is an act of worship (ibada). Dhimmis are not obligated to perform worship, so they cannot receive full shares. Women, children, and slaves may not fully participate in combat.
The ratio is that full shares are for those who actively engage in jihad as an act of worship.
5
Note the Discretionary Nature
The leader may choose to give radhakh or not; it is not wajib. This is why the hukm is mubah.
This distinguishes radhakh from sahm, which is wajib for eligible combatants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وللمملوك والمرأة والصبي والذمي الرضخ لا السهم) لأنه عليه السلام كان لا يسهم للنساء والصبيان والعبيد وكان يرضخ لهم ، ولما استعان النبي باليهود على اليهود لم يعطهم شيئاً من الغنيمة يعني لم يسهم لهم، ولأن الجهاد عبادة والذمي ليس من أهلها.
His statement: (And for the slave, woman, child, and dhimmi is radhakh, not the share) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not give shares to women, children, and slaves, but he would give them radhakh. And when the Prophet sought help from the Jews against the (other) Jews, he did not give them anything from the spoils, meaning he did not give them shares. And because jihad is an act of worship, and the dhimmi is not qualified for it.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This is a ruling that certain individuals are not entitled to a full share (sahm) in the spoils of war but may receive a discretionary grant (radhakh). The groups are: (1) slaves (mamluk), (2) women, (3) minors (sabi), and (4) dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens of the Islamic state). The proof is the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ), who did not allocate shares to women and children but gave them radhakh. Also, when the Prophet sought Jewish allies, he did not give them shares from the spoils, indicating that dhimmis are excluded. The reason is that jihad is an act of worship (ibada), and dhimmis are not qualified for worship, while women, children, and slaves may not be required or able to participate fully. Radhakh is given at the discretion of the leader.

Key Terms
الرضخ (al-radhakh): A small, discretionary grant given to those not entitled to a full share in spoils.
السهم (al-sahm): A fixed share in the spoils entitled to combatants (horsemen and foot soldiers).
الذمي (al-dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen living under the protection of an Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What do women, children, slaves, and dhimmis receive from the spoils?
A) A full share (sahm)
B) A small grant (radhakh)
C) Nothing
D) Double the share of a horseman

Key Takeaway
The leader gives radhakh to women, children, slaves, and dhimmis, not a full share, based on Prophetic practice.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
Reclaiming Captured Property Bought by a Trader
Detailed rulings on reclaiming captured property bought by a trader, with intra-Hanafi dispute on evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a trader buys captured property from the enemy and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whose evidence is preferred when the owner and trader dispute the price.

Core Idea
The owner must pay the trader's price to reclaim; if disputed, the owner's evidence prevails per the Sahibayn.

War booty and property captured by the enemy can lead to complex ownership issues when a Muslim trader buys it back. This lesson examines the rules for the original owner to reclaim such property and the nuances when the price is disputed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
The owner may take the property from the trader by paying the exact price the trader paid to the enemy. This prevents the trader from being harmed.
The ruling is a right, not an obligation.
2
Recognize the dispute on evidence
If owner and trader disagree on the price paid, and both present evidence, whose evidence is accepted? According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the owner's evidence is preferred. Abu Yusuf alone held the buyer's evidence is preferred.
The practical consequence: which price the owner pays.
3
Apply to invalid sale or payment with goods
If the sale was invalid (fasid), the owner takes the property at its own market value, not the price. If bought with goods (urud), the owner pays the value of those goods.
When the sale is valid but paid in goods, the owner pays the value of the goods.
4
Analyze the exception for identical property
If the trader bought an identical item (same quantity and quality), the owner cannot reclaim because there is no benefit (the owner gets back exactly what he lost). This applies to fungible goods (mithli).
No benefit means no harm to the trader, so no right to reclaim.
5
Resolve the conflict on wine/pig payment
If the trader bought the property with wine or a pig, the owner does not take it according to all narrations. However, the later scholars reconcile: if the property is fungible, the owner may take it by paying the value of the wine; if it is non-fungible (qimi), he pays its own value.
The mithli/qimi distinction resolves the apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وبالثمن لو اشتراه تاجر منهم) أي لو اشترى ما أخذه العدوّ منهم تاجر وأخرجه إلى دار الإسلام أخذه مالكه القديم بثمنه الذي اشترى به التاجر من العدو لأنه يتضرر بالأخذ مجاناً ألا ترى : أنه وقع العوض بمقابلته فكان اعتدال النظر فيما قلنا، ولو اختلف المولى والمشتري منهم في قدر الثمن فالقول قول المشتري بيمينه إلا أن يقيم المالك البينة؛ كذا في المحيط. وفي التتارخانية : وإن أقام أحدهما بينة قبلت وإن أقاما فعلى قولهما البينة بينة المولى القديم. وقال أبو يوسف بينة المشتري أراد بالثمن البدل فشمل ما إذا اشتراه بعرض فإنه يأخذه بقيمة العرض. ولو كان البيع فاسداً يأخذه بقيمة نفسه ويرد على المصنف ما لو اشتراه التاجر بمثله قدراً ووصفاً فإنه لا يأخذه المالك القديم لعدم الفائدة، سواء كان البيع صحيحاً أو فاسداً بخلاف ما إذا كان بأقل منه قدراً أو بأردأ منه وصفاً فإن له أن يأخذه لأنه مفيد ولا يكون رباً لأنه يستخلص ملكه فهو في الحقيقة فداء لا عوض، فلو كان اشتراه بمثله نسيئة فليس للمالك أخذه، ولو كان اشتراه بخمر أو خنزير لم يكن للمالك أخذه باتفاق الروايات. ولو أخذ المشركون ألف درهم نقد ببيت المال لرجل وأحرزوها فاشتراها التاجر درهم. غلة وتفرقوا عن قبض لم يكن للمالك أن يأخذها على الروايات كلها بمثل الغلة بألف لغيره فلا فإنا وجدناه صلح سبباً لكرامة تفوق الملك وهو الثواب كما في الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة فما ظنك بالملك الدنيوي؛ كذا في الفتح. قوله : (وفي التتارخانية وإن أقام أحدهما بينة الخ) قال فيها بعد هذه المسألة : هذا الذي ذكرنا كله إذا اختلفا في مقدار الثمن الذي اشتراه المشتري من العدو، أما إذا اختلفا في مقدار قيمة العوض الذي اشتراه من العدو وأقاما جميعاً البينة ذكر محمد أن البينة بيئة المشتري من العدو وقال : وهذا قول أبي يوسف ولم يذكر قول أبي حنيفة في هذه المسألة اهـ. قوله : (لم يكن للمالك أخذه قال في النهر : يعني بالخمر والخنزير ومقتضى ما أنه يأخذه بقيمة نفسه وبه صرح في السراج .اهـ. وعبارة صاحب السراج في الجوهرة: وإن اشتراه بخمر أو خنزير
منهم
أخذه بقيمة الخمر وإن شاء تركه انتهت وفي التتارخانية : ولو كان المشتري اشترى هذا الكر بخمر أو خنزير وأخرجه إلى دار الإسلام لم يكن للمالك القديم أن يأخذه على الروايات كلها اهـ. والذي يظهر أن المبيع إن كان مثلياً أخذه بقيمة ،الخمر وإن كان قيمياً فبقيمته نفسه. والأول محمل كلام الجوهرة، والثاني محمل كلام السراج ولا ينافيه ما في التتارخانية فتأمل وراجع.
His statement: 'And with the price if a trader bought from them' means: if a trader bought what the enemy took from them and brought it to Dar al-Islam, its old owner takes it with the price that the trader bought from the enemy, because he would be harmed by taking it for free. Do you not see that the consideration occurred in exchange for it, so judicial consideration is as we said. And if the owner and the buyer from them dispute over the amount of the price, the statement is the buyer's with his oath unless the owner provides evidence; thus in al-Muhit. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: And if one of them provides evidence, it is accepted; and if both provide evidence, according to both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the evidence is the evidence of the old owner. Abu Yusuf said: the evidence of the buyer; he meant by price the equivalent, so it includes if he bought it with goods, then he takes it with the value of the goods. And if the sale was invalid, he takes it with its own value. And it is objected to the author: what if the trader bought it with the like in quantity and quality? Then the old owner does not take it due to lack of benefit, whether the sale is valid or invalid. But if it is less in quantity or inferior in quality, then he may take it because it is beneficial and it is not usury, because he is reclaiming his ownership; it is in reality a redemption, not a compensation. So if he bought it with the like on credit, the owner does not take it. And if he bought it with wine or a pig, the owner does not take it by agreement of the narrations. And if the idolaters took one thousand dirhams in cash from the treasury of a man and secured them, and the trader bought them with [something],... 
His statement: 'And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: And if one of them provides evidence, etc.' He said in it after this issue: All that we mentioned is when they dispute over the amount of the price that the buyer bought from the enemy. But if they dispute over the amount of the value of the consideration that he bought from the enemy, and both provide evidence, Muhammad mentioned that the evidence is the evidence of the buyer from the enemy, and he said: This is the statement of Abu Yusuf, and he did not mention the statement of Abu Hanifa in this issue. End. His statement: 'He does not take it' – he said in al-Nahr: meaning with wine and pig; and the requirement is that he takes it with its own value, and that is explicit in al-Siraj. End. And the statement of the author of al-Siraj in al-Jawhara: And if he bought it with wine or a pig, he takes it with the value of the wine and if he wishes he leaves it. End. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: And if the buyer bought this kurr with wine or a pig and brought it to Dar al-Islam, the old owner does not take it according to all the narrations. End. And what appears is that if the sale item is fungible (mithli), he takes it with the value of the wine; if it is non-fungible (qimi), then with its own value. The first is the interpretation of the statement of al-Jawhara, and the second is the interpretation of al-Siraj, and it does not contradict what is in al-Tatarkhaniyya, so contemplate and refer back.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'And with the price if a trader bought from them.' It states that if a Muslim trader buys captured property from the enemy and brings it to Dar al-Islam, the original (pre-capture) owner may reclaim it by paying the exact price the trader paid. This is because the trader would suffer harm if the owner took it for free, as the trader gave consideration. The passage then addresses disputes: if the owner and trader disagree on the price, the trader's word is taken with an oath unless the owner has evidence. This is from al-Muhit. The Tatarkhaniyya adds that if both provide evidence, the owner's evidence is preferred according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), though Abu Yusuf elsewhere preferred the buyer's evidence. If the sale was invalid (fasid), the owner takes the property at its own value (value of the item itself, not the price). However, if the trader bought an identical item (same in quantity and quality), the owner cannot reclaim because there is no benefit (the owner would get back exactly what he lost, so no harm). This applies whether the sale is valid or invalid. But if the item is less in quantity or inferior, the owner may take it because it is beneficial. The passage also discusses payment with wine or pig: if the trader bought with wine or pig, the owner does not take it by consensus of narrations. Further, if the enemy took money from a man's treasury and the trader bought it with something like dates? (the text is corrupt), the owner cannot reclaim. The later part of the passage resolves a conflict between al-Jawhara and al-Siraj regarding whether the owner takes the item with the value of the wine or the value of the item itself: the answer is that if the item is fungible (mithli), the owner takes it with the value of the wine; if non-fungible (qimi), with its own value.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute, compensation; here it refers to the price or equivalent value paid by the trader.
مثلي (mithli): Fungible good that can be replaced by an identical item (e.g., grain, money).
قيمي (qimi): Non-fungible good that has no exact equivalent (e.g., a specific animal or item).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute between the old owner and the buyer about the price paid to the enemy, which party's evidence is preferred according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)?
A) The buyer's evidence.
B) The old owner's evidence.
C) Neither, the judge decides.
D) The evidence of a third party.

Key Takeaway
The original owner reclaims captured property by paying the trader's price; when disputed, the owner's evidence is preferred per the Sahibayn.

Gouging the Eye of a Purchased Slave: Price Reduction or Not?
Explains compensation when slave's eye is gouged by purchaser.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on price reduction when a purchased slave's eye is gouged, distinguish it from pre-emption, and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
In a valid sale, damage to an attribute does not reduce the price; the owner compensates from the gouger.

When a slave captured in war is sold and then his eye is gouged, does the purchaser get a price reduction? The Hanafi school has an internal debate: the relied-upon view says no reduction, while a narration from Imam Muhammad says yes, by analogy to pre-emption. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning (talil) and the distinction between valid and defective ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State the exact ruling: the purchaser does not reduce the price and the original owner does not take the compensation from the purchaser.
This is the main ruling from the passage.
2
Understand the principle
Why no reduction? Because attributes (like the eye) are not compensated by a portion of the price in a valid sale after possession.
This principle distinguishes from pre-emption.
3
Contrast with pre-emption (shuf'a)
In pre-emption, if the purchaser demolishes a building, the price is reduced for the pre-emptor because the purchase is considered defective (like a corrupt sale).
Here ownership is valid, so different ruling.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and the two companions agree on no price reduction but differ on who takes compensation from the gouger. Imam Muhammad has a narration that the price reduces proportionally.
The ikhtilaf: value taken (blind vs sound) and whether reduction occurs.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is no price reduction, as preferred by al-Hidayah and al-Bahr al-Raiq.
The distinction between this case and pre-emption is considered correct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ندعينه كانت عينه فقئت وأخذ التاجر أرشها يعنى لا يحط شيئاً من الثمن ولا يأخذ المالك الأرش. أما الأول فلأن الأوصاف لا يقابلها شيء من الثمن بخلاف الشفعة لأن الصفقة لما تحولت إلى الشفيع صار المشتري في يد المشتري بمنزلة المشتري شراء فاسداً والأوصاف تضمن فيه كما في الغصب، أما هنا الملك صحيح فافترقا وأما الثاني فلأن الملك فيه صحيح فلو أخذه أخذه بمثله وهو لا يفيد وظاهر ما في فتح القدير أن الفاقئ غير التاجر فإنه قال : ولو أنه فقأ عند الغازي المقسوم له فأخذ قيمته وسلمه للفاقئ فللمالك الأول أخذه من الفاقئ بقيمته أعمى عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا بقيمته سليماً وهي التي أعطاها الفاقئ للمولى. والفرق لأبي حنيفة أن فوات الطرف هنا بفعل الذي ملكه باختياره فكان بمنزلة ما لو اشتراه سليماً ثم قطع طرفه باختياره فكان راضياً بتنقيصه بخلاف مسألة الكتاب لأن الفاقئ غيره بغير رضاه اهـ . وصرح في المحيط بأن المشتري إذا فقأ عينها فالحكم كذلك. وعن محمد أنه تسقط حصته من الثمن، وهذا بمنزلة الشفعة إذا هدم المشتري البناء سقط عن الشفيع حصة البناء فكذا هذا اهـ. فعلى رواية محمد لا فرق بين مسألة الكتاب والشفعة إذ الوصف لا يقابله شيء إلا إذا صار مقصوداً بالإتلاف وهو موافق لما ذكروه في البيوع لكن ظاهر الهداية الفرق بين الكتاب والشفعة وهو الحق. ولا فرق في الفاقئ بين أن يكون التاجر أو غيره ولهذا قال الشارح: : الأوصاف لا يقابلها شيء من الثمن في ملك صحيح بعد القبض وإن كانت مقصودة بالإتلاف بخلاف المشفوع لأن شراءه من غير رضا الشفيع مكروه وملكه ينتقض من غير رضاه فأشبه البيع الفاسد اهـ . ولو أخرجه المشتري من ملکه بعوض يأخذه العدو عن المالك القديم بذلك العوض إن كان مالاً، وإن كان غير مال كالصلح عن دم أو هبة أخذه بقيمته ولا ينتقض تصرفه بخلاف الشفيع لأن حقه قبل حق المشتري فينتقض تصرف المشتري لأجله، والتقييد بالعين اتفاقي لأن اليد لو قطعت فالحكم كذلك. ولو ولدت الجارية عند المشتري فأعتق المشتري أحدهما أخذ الباقي منهما بجميع الثمن لأن الفداء لا يتوزع ما بقي شيء من الأصل أو ما تولد منه، وعن محمد إن أعتق الأم أخذ الولد بحصته من الثمن وليس الولد كالأرش؛ كذا في المحيط . وفي المغرب : فقأ العين غارها بأن شق حدقتها، والقلع أن ينزع حدقتها بعروقها والأرش دية الجراحات والجمع أروش اهـ.
And if his eye was gouged, and the trader took its compensation, meaning he does not reduce anything from the price, nor does the owner take the compensation. As for the first, because attributes are not compensated by anything from the price, unlike pre-emption because when the transaction transfers to the pre-emptor, the purchaser is in the hand of the purchaser like a purchaser with a corrupt sale, and attributes are guaranteed therein as in usurpation. But here the ownership is valid, so they differ. As for the second, because ownership therein is valid, so if he takes it, he takes it equivalent to it, which is useless. And apparent from Fath al-Qadeer that the gouger is other than the trader, for he said: If he gouged the eye of the one divided to the soldier, and he took its value and handed it to the gouger, then the first owner takes it from the gouger for its value blind according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: for its value sound, which is what the gouger gave to the owner. The distinction for Abu Hanifa is that the loss of the limb here is by the act of the one who owned it with his choice, so it is like if he bought it sound then cut its limb with his choice, thus he was content with its diminution, unlike the issue of the book because the gouger is someone else without his consent. And it is stated in al-Muhit that if the purchaser gouges its eye, the ruling is the same. And from Muhammad that his portion of the price drops, and this is like pre-emption: if the purchaser demolishes the building, the share of the building drops from the pre-emptor. So according to Muhammad's narration, there is no difference between the issue of the book and pre-emption, since the attribute is not compensated except when it becomes intended by destruction, and that agrees with what they mentioned in sales, but the apparent of al-Hidayah is the difference between the book and pre-emption, and it is correct. And there is no difference in the gouger whether it is the trader or someone else, hence the commentator said: Attributes are not compensated by anything from the price in valid ownership after possession, even if they are intended by destruction, unlike the pre-empted property because his purchase without the pre-emptor's consent is disliked and his ownership is invalidated without his consent, so it resembles a corrupt sale. And if the purchaser removes it from his ownership for compensation, the enemy takes it from the original owner for that compensation if it is property, and if it is not property like reconciliation for blood or a gift, he takes it for its value, and his transaction is not invalidated unlike the pre-emptor because his right is before the right of the purchaser, so the purchaser's transaction is invalidated for his sake. And the restriction to the eye is incidental, because if the hand is cut, the ruling is the same. And if the slave-girl gives birth with the purchaser, and the purchaser frees one of them, he takes the remaining one from them for the entire price because the ransom is not distributed. There remains something from the original or what is born from it. And from Muhammad, if he freed the mother, he takes the child for its portion of the price, and the child is not like the compensation. In al-Muhit. And in al-Mughrib: Fiq' al-ayn is to gouge it by slitting its socket, and al-qal' is to pull out its socket with its roots, and al-arsh is the blood money for wounds, plural arush.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling when the eye of a captured slave is gouged after purchase from the enemy. The commentator begins by stating the ruling: the trader does not reduce the price nor does the owner take the compensation. The reason is that attributes (like eye, hand) are not compensated by a portion of the price in a valid sale, unlike pre-emption where the purchaser's ownership is defective. The commentary then contrasts the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions regarding who can take compensation. Abu Hanifa holds that if the gouger is not the purchaser, the original owner can take the blind slave but only for its decreased value, because the loss was by an act of a non-owner. The two companions say the owner can take it for full sound value. The distinction hinges on consent: Abu Hanifa argues that since the purchaser owned the slave by choice, any damage by him is deemed consented to. A narration from Muhammad suggests that the price is proportionally reduced, analogous to pre-emption when a building is demolished. However, the preferred view (from al-Hidayah) maintains the difference between this case and pre-emption. The passage then expands to other scenarios: if the purchaser sells the slave to the enemy, the original owner takes it for that price; if a gift, for value. If the slave gives birth, the whole offspring goes with the mother. The final lines provide linguistic definitions of fqa' and arsh.

Key Terms
فقأ العين (faq' al-ayn): Gouging the eye by slitting the socket; a specific type of injury.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for wounds or loss of a limb, determined by the type of injury.
شفعة (shuf'a): Pre-emption right of a co-owner to purchase a sold share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, what happens if the purchaser gouges the eye of a slave purchased from the enemy?
A) The price is reduced by the value of the eye.
B) The original owner can take the slave without paying anything.
C) The purchaser does not reduce the price and the owner takes compensation from the gouger.
D) The sale is invalidated.

Key Takeaway
In a valid sale, damage to an attribute does not reduce the price; the owner must seek compensation from the tortfeasor directly.

Rights of Buyers and Original Owner in Repeated Slave Capture
Explains rights of owners when a slave is captured and sold multiple times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of rights when a slave is captured and purchased twice, and apply the rule to determine who may take the slave from whom.

Core Idea
The first purchaser, not the original owner, directly recovers from the second; the original owner then recovers from the first by paying both prices.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific but instructive case: a slave is captured and sold, then captured again and sold to a different buyer. The commentator clarifies the layered rights of the original owner, the first buyer, and the second buyer. Understanding this chain of recovery reveals how Hanafi fiqh protects ownership continuity through multiple involuntary transfers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and events
There are three parties: the original owner (malik qadim), the first purchaser (mushtari awwal), and the second purchaser (mushtari thani). Two separate captures and two separate sales occur.
2
Determine who may take the slave from the second purchaser
The text states the first purchaser may take the slave from the second purchaser by paying the second's price. The original owner cannot do so directly.
The reason is that the second capture occurred while the slave was owned by the first purchaser, not the original owner.
3
Trace the original owner's right to recover
Once the first purchaser recovers the slave, he has incurred two prices (his own purchase price and the amount paid to the second). The original owner may now take the slave from the first purchaser by paying both prices.
This is because the first purchaser's right to take is a form of liberation that makes him liable for the two prices.
4
Note the exceptions and the intra-Hanafi difference
If capture is not repeated (only one capture), the original owner may go directly to the second buyer. There is also a narration from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (via Ibn Sama'a) that allows the original owner to nullify the second contract, but the relied-upon view is the first narration.
This difference illustrates the importance of tarjih (preference) within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة قوله : ( فإن تكرر الأسر والشراء أخذ الأول من الثاني بثمنه ثم القديم بالثمنين) يعني لو أسر العبد مرتين واشتراه في المرأة الأولى رجل وفي الثانية رجل آخر كان حق الأخذ من المشتري الثاني للمشتري الأول بما اشترى لأن الأسر ورد على ملكة وأفاد أنه ليس للمالك القديم أن يأخذه من المشتري الثاني ولو كان المشتري الأول غائباً أو كان حاضراً إلا أنه أبى عن أخذه لأن الأسر ما ورد على ملكه فإذا أخذه المشتري الأول من الثاني بثمنه فقد قام عليه بالثمنين فكان للمالك القديم أن يأخذ بالثمنين إن شاء من المشتري الأول لأنه قام عليه بهما. وأفاد بتعبيره بالأخذ المفيد للتخليص أن المشتري الأول لو اشتراه من الثاني ليس للقديم الأخذ ثبت للمالك القديم في ضمن عود ملك المشتري الأول ولم يعد ملكه القديم وإنما ملكه بالشراء الجديد منه. وقيد بتكرر الشراء لأن المشتري الأول لو كان وهبه له أخذه مولاه من الموهوب له بقيمته كما لو وهب الكافر المسلم. وقيد بتكرر الأسر لأنه لو لم يتكرر كما إذا باع المشتري من العدو والعبد من غيره أخذه المالك القديم من الثاني بالثمن الذي اشتراه به إن مثلياً فبمثله وإن قيمياً بأن كان اشتراه مقايضة فبقيمته لأن المشتري الثاني قائم مقام المشتري الأول، وليس للقديم أن ينقض العقد الثاني فيأخذه من المشتري الأول بالثمن للمولى إلا رواية ابن سماعة عن محمد وظاهر الرواية الأولى والوجه في المبسوط
Issue: His statement: (If capture and purchase are repeated, the first takes from the second by his price, then the old (original owner) by two prices) meaning if the slave is captured twice, and in the first instance a man bought him, and in the second another man, the right to take from the second purchaser belongs to the first purchaser by what he bought, because the capture occurred on his ownership, and it indicates that the old owner cannot take him from the second purchaser, even if the first purchaser is absent or present but refuses to take him, because the capture did not occur on his ownership. So when the first purchaser takes him from the second by his price, he has incurred two prices, so the old owner may take him by the two prices if he wishes from the first purchaser because he incurred them. And by his expression 'taking' meaning extraction, if the first purchaser buys him from the second, the old owner does not have the right to take; the old owner's right is established within the return of the first purchaser's ownership, and his old ownership does not return; rather he owns it by new purchase from him. And he restricted by repetition of purchase, because if the first purchaser had gifted him to him, his owner takes him from the donee by his value, as if a disbeliever gifted a Muslim. And he restricted by repetition of capture, because if it were not repeated, as when the purchaser sold to the enemy and the slave from someone else, the old owner takes him from the second by the price he bought him for – if it is a fungible, by its like; if it is a non-fungible, as if he bought him by exchange, then by its value – because the second purchaser stands in place of the first purchaser, and the old owner cannot nullify the second contract to take him from the first purchaser by the price for the owner, except according to the narration of Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad, and the apparent first narration and the correct view in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning on repeated capture and purchase of a slave. The commentator explains the rule from the matn: if a slave is captured twice and purchased each time, the first buyer can take the slave from the second buyer by paying the second buyer's price. Then the original owner can take the slave from the first buyer by two prices (the first and second prices). The commentary justifies this by noting that the first capture occurred on the original owner's property, so the original owner cannot go directly to the second buyer; only the first buyer has that right. However, once the first buyer retrieves the slave, he incurs two prices, so the original owner can now take from him by paying both. The passage also covers exceptions: if the first buyer gifted the slave, the original owner takes by value; if the capture was not repeated (single capture), the original owner can go directly to the second buyer. The final part mentions a narration from Muhammad via Ibn Sama'a that differs on whether the original owner can nullify the second contract.

Key Terms
الأسر (al-asr): Capture by the enemy, which can transfer ownership.
الثمن (al-thaman): The price paid in a sale; here refers to the purchase price from the enemy.
القديم (al-qadim): The original owner before the first capture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a case of repeated capture and purchase, who can directly take the slave from the second purchaser?
A) The original owner.
B) The first purchaser.
C) Either the original owner or the first purchaser.
D) Only the second purchaser's owner.

Key Takeaway
The right of recovery follows the ownership at the time of each capture; the original owner cannot bypass the first purchaser.

The Prohibition on a Muslim Musta'min Harming Harbis
Ruling on a Muslim musta'min's obligations in dar al-harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling on a Muslim musta'min harming harbis and identify the exceptions when harm is permitted.

Core Idea
A Muslim musta'min in dar al-harb is forbidden from harming harbis unless they betray him first.

When a Muslim trader enters dar al-harb with an aman (safe conduct), he is bound by a contract of protection. This lesson explores the default prohibition against harming harbi persons or property, the exceptions when the harbi king betrays, and the distinction between a musta'min and a captive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the default hukm for a Muslim musta'min harming harbi persons or property.
Default is haram.
2
Understand the rationale
The aman contract imposes a guarantee; harming after aman is treachery (ghadr), which is haram.
Treachery is prohibited by consensus.
3
Note the exception
If the harbi king betrays the musta'min (by seizing property, imprisonment, etc.), the aman is broken and harming is permitted.
Betrayal nullifies the contract.
4
Distinguish the captive
A captive released without aman is not a musta'min; he may harm harbis like a sneak thief.
Captive is not bound by aman.
5
Apply to specific cases
Consider property, family members, and captured Muslim children; the ruling varies based on ownership and the nature of the aman.
See the branches from al-Mabsut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المستأمن
دخل تاجرنا ثم حرم تعرضه لشيء منهم فلو أخرج شيئاً ملكه ملكاً محظوراً دارنا فإن حكمه أن يبيعه الإمام ويحفظ ثمنه لمولاه الحربي لأنه لما دخل بأمان صارت رقبته داخلة فيه كما لو دخل سيده به وبما معه من المال. وفي شرح الطحاوي: ولا يثبت ولاء العبد الخارج إلينا مسلماً لأحد لأن هذا عتق حكمي والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
باب المستأمن
أخره عن الاستيلاء لأن الاستيلاء يكون بالقهر والاستئمان يكون بعد القهر قوله : (دخل تاجرنا ثم حرم تعرضه لشيء منهم) أي دخل المسلم دار الحرب بأمان، وعبر عنه بالتاجر لأنه لا يدخل دارهم إلا بأمان حفظاً لما له وإنما حرم عليه لأنه ضمن بالاستثمان أن لا يتعرض لهم فالتعرض بعد ذلك يكون غدراً والغدر حرام إلا إذا غدر به ملكهم فأخذ ماله أو حبسه أو فعل غيره بعلم الملك ولم يمنعه لأنهم هم الذين نقضوا العهد. قيد بالتاجر لأن الأسير يباح له التعرض وإن أطلقوه طوعاً لأنه غير مستأمن فهو كالمتلصص فيجوز له أخذ المال وقتل النفس دون استباحة الفرج لأنه لا يحل إلا بالملك ولا ملك قبل الإحراز بدارنا إلا إذا وجد من لم يملكه أهل الحرب من امرأته وأم ولده ومدبرته فيباح له وطؤهن إلا إذا وطئهن أهل الحرب فتجب العدة للشبهة فلا يجوز وطؤهن حتى تنقضي عدتهن بخلاف أمته المأسورة لا يحل وطؤها مطلقاً لأنها مملوكة لهم. وأطلق الشيء فشمل النفوس والأموال حتى أمة التاجر المأسورة لأنها من أملاكهم، ولا يدخل تحته زوجته وأم ولده ومدبرته لأنهن غير مملوكات لهم فيجوز للتاجر التعرض لهن، وكذا لو أغار أهل الحرب الذين فيهم مسلمون مستأمنون على طائفة من المسلمين فأسروا ذراريهم فمروا بهم على أولئك المستأمنين وجب عليهم أن ينقضوا عهودهم ويقاتلوهم إذا كانوا يقدرون عليه لأنهم لا يملكون رقابهم فتقريرهم في أيديهم تقرير على الظلم، ولم يضمنوا ذلك لهم بخلاف الأموال لأنهم ملكوها بالإحراز وقد ضمنوا لهم أن لا يتعرضوا لأموالهم، وكذا لو كان المأخوذ ذراري الخوارج لأنهم مسلمون. ومن الفروع النفيسة ما في المبسوط : لو أغار قوم من أهل الحرب على أهل الدار التي فيهم المسلم المستأمن لا يحل له قتال هؤلاء الكفار إلا إن خاف على نفسه لأن
باب المستأمن
قوله : (والظاهر عدم تخصيصه بالبيع وأنه لا يشمل القرض كذا في بعض النسخ وفي بعضها
Chapter of Musta'min. Our trader enters, then it is forbidden to harm anything of them. So if he takes out something he owns as forbidden property to our abode, then its ruling is that the Imam sells it and preserves its price for his harbi master, because when he entered with aman, his neck became included in it, just as if his master entered with him and with what he had of wealth. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: No wala' is established for the slave who comes out to us as a Muslim to anyone, because this is a constructive manumission. And Allah knows best. Chapter of Musta'min. He delayed it after domination because domination is by force and musta'min is after force. He said: (Our trader enters, then it is forbidden to harm anything of them) meaning the Muslim enters dar al-harb with aman, and he is called a trader because he does not enter their abode except with aman to preserve his property. It is forbidden for him because he guaranteed by the aman that he would not harm them, so harming after that is treachery, and treachery is forbidden unless their king betrays him by taking his money or imprisoning him or doing other things with the king's knowledge and he does not prevent him, because they are the ones who broke the covenant. It is restricted to the trader because the captive is permitted to harm them even if they release him willingly, because he is not musta'min; he is like a sneak thief, so it is permissible for him to take property and kill lives without making lawful sexual intercourse, because that is not lawful except by ownership, and there is no ownership before taking possession in our abode, except if he finds what the people of war do not own: his wife, his umm walad, and his mudabbara; it is permissible for him to have intercourse with them, unless the people of war have had intercourse with them, then iddah is required due to shubha, so it is not permissible to have intercourse until their iddah expires, unlike his captured slave girl; it is not permissible to have intercourse with her at all because she is owned by them. And he mentioned 'thing' generally, so it includes lives and wealth, even the captured slave girl of the trader because she is from their property. But it does not include his wife, umm walad, and mudabbara because they are not owned by them, so the trader may harm them (take them). Likewise, if the people of war who have Muslim musta'mins among them raid a group of Muslims and capture their children and then pass by those musta'mins, it is obligatory for them to break their covenant and fight them if they are able, because they do not own their necks, so keeping them in their hands is oppression. And they are not liable for that to them, unlike property, because they own it by possession and they have guaranteed not to harm their property. Likewise, if the captives are children of the Khawarij because they are Muslims. Among the valuable branches in al-Mabsut: If a group of people of war raid the people of a house in which there is a Muslim musta'min, it is not permissible for him to fight these disbelievers unless he fears for himself because... Chapter of Musta'min. He said: (And it appears it is not restricted to sale and it does not include loan, as in some copies, and in some copies...
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This section, 'Chapter of Musta'min', deals with the legal status of a Muslim who enters dar al-harb under an aman (safe conduct). The matn states: 'Our trader enters, then it is forbidden to harm anything of them.' The commentary explains that a Muslim trader enters dar al-harb with aman to protect his property. He is prohibited from harming any harbi person or property because by accepting aman he has guaranteed their safety. Harming them would be treachery (ghadr), which is forbidden. However, if the harbi king himself betrays the Muslim (e.g., by seizing his property or imprisoning him), then the aman is broken, and the Muslim may retaliate. The commentary distinguishes the trader from a captive (asir): a captive who is released is not a musta'min, so he may harm the harbis like a sneak thief. He may take their property and even kill them, but he cannot have intercourse with their women because that requires ownership, which is not established until the property is brought to dar al-Islam. An exception is made for a Muslim's wife, umm walad, or mudabbara who are not owned by the harbis; if the Muslim finds them, he may have intercourse with them, provided they have not been sexually violated by harbis (in which case iddah is required). A captured slave girl of the Muslim is owned by the harbis, so intercourse is forbidden. The commentary also discusses the duty of Muslim musta'mins when they see harbis capturing Muslim children: they must break their aman and fight to rescue them, because the children are not owned by the harbis. This does not apply to property, which the harbis own by possession. The same applies to children of the Khawarij (a deviant Muslim sect), as they are still Muslims. Finally, a branch from al-Mabsut: if harbis raid a house where a Muslim musta'min is present, he may not fight them unless he fears for his own life. The passage ends with a note on a textual variant regarding whether the ruling is restricted to sale or includes loan.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A Muslim who enters dar al-harb with a safe conduct (aman).
غدر (ghadr): Treachery or breach of a pledge, which is haram.
إحراز (ihraz): Taking possession or bringing into one's safe custody, especially property taken from dar al-harb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible for a Muslim musta'min in dar al-harb to take property from the harbis?
A) At any time, because harbi property is always lawful.
B) Only if the harbi king betrays him first.
C) Only if he is a captive, not a trader.
D) He may take property only if he fears for his life.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim musta'min is bound by aman to refrain from harming harbis; only betrayal by the harbi king or self-defense permits retaliation.

Why Arab Lands Are Tithe Lands (ʻUshriyyah)
Ruling with proof on the classification of Arab lands as tithe lands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Arab lands are ʻushriyyah, explain the proof from the practice of the Prophet and caliphs, and rebut the objection from al-Bināyah.

Core Idea
Arab lands are tithe lands because kharāj was never taken from them, and its imposition requires the inhabitants to remain in disbelief.

This lesson examines the first category mentioned in the matn: 'The land of the Arabs is tithe land.' The commentator provides the proof from the continuous practice of the Prophet and caliphs, and addresses a criticism regarding the absence of a specific hadith. Understanding this ruling is essential for classifying land and determining the wajib levy on its produce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
From the matn, state that Arab lands are classified as ʻushriyyah (tithe land). Note also the other two categories: land whose inhabitants accepted Islam, and land conquered by force and divided among the spoils.
2
Examine the Proof
The proof for Arab lands is that the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs never took kharāj from them. The commentator argues this absence of transmission is itself evidence.
This is a dalīl ʻadami (evidence from absence).
3
Address the Criticism
Al-Bināyah objected that this has no basis in hadith books. The response is that if kharāj had been taken, it would have been transmitted; therefore, the absence of reports indicates the absence of the practice.
4
Understand the Legal Rationale
Kharāj is only imposed when the inhabitants remain upon disbelief. Arab polytheists had no option but to accept Islam or be killed, so kharāj cannot apply. This is the reason why Arab lands are exclusively ʻushriyyah.

Source Text

باب العشر والخراج والجزية

Chapter of Tithe, Land Tax, and Jizya
Explanation of what is taken from the dhimmi after explaining what makes him a dhimmi, and mentioning the tithe is a completion of financial obligations, and it is given precedence due to the element of worship. The tithe (al-ʻushr) with a ḍammah on the ʻayn is the singular of al-ʻusharah, and al-kharāj is the name for what is extracted from the produce of land or a boy, then it is used for what the ruler takes as land tax; it is said: So-and-so paid the land tax of his land. His statement: (The land of the Arabs and what its inhabitants accepted Islam or was conquered by force and divided among the spoils is tithe land). As for the land of the Arabs, because the Prophet (ﷺ) and the Rightly Guided Caliphs (may Allah be pleased with them all) did not take land tax from the land of the Arabs. It was criticized in al-Bināyah that this has no basis in hadith books, and he did not respond to it. The response is that absence does not require a basis, because if they had taken land tax from them, it would have been transmitted, and since it is not transmitted, it indicates its absence. And because it is like war booty, so it is not established on their lands just as it is not established on their persons. This is because the condition for imposing land tax is that the inhabitants remain upon disbelief, as in the Sawād of Iraq, and the polytheists of the Arabs are only accepted with Islam or the sword. It is mentioned in al-Maghrib with attribution to the Book of Tithe and Land Tax: Abu Yusuf in al-Amālī: The boundaries of the land of the Arabs are what lies beyond the boundaries of the land of Kufa to the farthest rock in Yemen. And from Muhammad: from ʻAdan Abyan to Syria and what borders it. In Sharḥ al-Qudūrī, al-Karkhī said: It is the land of Hijaz, Tihamah, Yemen, Mecca, al-Ṭāʼif, and al-Bariyyah meaning the desert. He said: And Muhammad said: The land of the Arabs is from al-ʻUdhayb to Mecca and ʻAdan Abyan to the farthest stone in Yemen in Mahrah. These statements I have not found in language books, and it is clear that whoever narrated 'to the farthest stone (ḥajar)' with sukun and interpreted it as 'side' has altered it because the word 'rock (ṣakhr)' occurs in its place, and it seems they mentioned it as an emphasis on the limit, otherwise he could dispense with it. End from al-Maghrib. And 'Jazirat al-ʻArab' means its land and its settlement. In al-Bināyah: al-ʻUdhayb - with ḍammah on the ʻayn and fatḥah on the dhāl and muʻjamah and with bāʼ mawḥḥidah - is a water source for Tamīm. And al-Ḥajar - with two fatḥahs - meaning rock, and Mahrah - with fatḥah on the haa and sukun - is the name of a man, and it is said...
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It opens the chapter on tithe, land tax, and jizya. The author (Zaylaʻi) first defines the terms: al-ʻushr (tithe) is singular of 'usharah, and al-kharāj is the produce extracted from land or even a boy, but here it refers to what the ruler collects from land. The matn statement from Kanz al-Daqāʼiq declares: 'The land of the Arabs, and whatever land whose inhabitants accepted Islam, or was conquered by force and divided among the spoils, is tithe land (ʻushriyyah).' The commentary explains that Arab lands are tithe lands because the Prophet and the caliphs never took kharāj from them. A criticism from al-Bināyah that this has no hadith basis is answered by saying that absence of evidence is evidence of absence – if kharāj had been taken, it would have been reported. Moreover, kharāj is only justified when the inhabitants remain kuffār, but Arab polytheists had no option but Islam or death, so kharāj cannot be imposed on them. The passage then provides geographical definitions of Arab lands from various authorities: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Karkhī, and others, with locations like al-ʻUdhayb, ʻAdan Abyan, etc. The commentary notes these definitions are not found in standard language books.

Key Terms
العشر (al-ʻushr): Tithe, a 10% levy on agricultural produce from land classified as ʻushriyyah.
الخراج (al-kharāj): Land tax imposed on kharājī lands, typically a fixed annual amount or a share of produce, taken from non-Muslim inhabitants or owners.
العنوة (al-ʻanwah): Conquest by force, as opposed to ṣulḥ (treaty).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are Arab lands classified as ʻushriyyah rather than kharājiyyah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the Prophet ﷺ explicitly said so in a hadith.
B) Because the caliphs imposed kharāj on them.
C) Because kharāj is only imposed when the inhabitants remain upon disbelief, which was not an option for Arab polytheists.
D) Because all lands conquered by force are automatically ʻushriyyah.

Key Takeaway
Arab lands are exclusively tithe lands (ʻushriyyah) because the Prophet and caliphs never took kharāj from them, and kharāj cannot be imposed when the inhabitants must either accept Islam or be killed.

Geographical Boundaries of Arab Lands in Hanafi Fiqh
Expansion on the geographical boundaries of Arab lands, extracted from Hanafi authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the various definitions of Arab lands given by Hanafi jurists (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Karkhi) and explain the significance of these boundaries for the classification of land as ʻushri.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school defines Arab lands with specific geographical markers, and these definitions determine which lands are subject to ʻushr instead of kharāj.

This lesson examines the second part of the passage, where the commentator extracts the geographical boundaries of Arab lands from several Hanafi authorities. Understanding these boundaries is crucial for applying the ruling that Arab lands are ʻushriyyah. The lesson will also address a textual issue regarding the transmission of one of these boundaries.

Guided Path
1
List the Definitions
Identify the three definitions provided: Abu Yusuf's, Muhammad's (first), and al-Karkhi's (with Muhammad's second). Note the reference sources.
Abu Yusuf: from al-Amālī; Muhammad: from al-Maghrib; al-Karkhi: in Sharḥ al-Qudūrī.
2
Compare the Definitions
Compare the boundaries: Are they consistent? What does each definition include? Note that they all include Yemen, Hijaz, etc., but differ in starting points.
Main differences: Abu Yusuf starts from beyond Kufa; Muhammad starts from ʻAdan Abyan; al-Karkhi includes Hijaz, Tihamah, etc.
3
Analyze the Textual Issue
The commentator notes a confusion in the transmission of Muhammad's definition: 'to the farthest stone' (ḥajar) vs. 'rock' (ṣakhr). Explain the correction.
The correct word is 'ṣakhr' (rock), not 'ḥajar' (stone).
4
Understand the Purpose
Why did the jurists provide these boundaries? The commentator says it is to emphasize the limit, even if it is not necessary. The boundaries confirm that Arab lands are extensive and well-known.
The boundaries are not exhaustive but serve as guidance for practical application.

كتاب السير باب العشر والخراج والجزية
۱۷۷
وما فتح عنوة وأقر أهله عليه أو فتح صلحاً خراجية ولو أحيا أرضاً مواتا يعتبر قربه
اسم قبيلة ينسب إليها الإبل المهرية، وسمي ذلك المقام به فيكون «بمهرة» بدلاً من قوله «باليمن» اهـ . وأما إذا أسلم أهلها أو فتحت قهراً وقسمت بين الغانمين فلأن الحاجة إلى ابتداء التوظيف على المسلم والعشر أليق به لما فيه من معنى العبادة وكذا هو أحق حيث يتعلق بنفس الخارج والعنوة بالفتح القهر ؛ كذا في المغرب.
Chapter of Tithe, Land Tax, and Jizya
Explanation of what is taken from the dhimmi after explaining what makes him a dhimmi, and mentioning the tithe is a completion of financial obligations, and it is given precedence due to the element of worship. The tithe (al-ʻushr) with a ḍammah on the ʻayn is the singular of al-ʻusharah, and al-kharāj is the name for what is extracted from the produce of land or a boy, then it is used for what the ruler takes as land tax; it is said: So-and-so paid the land tax of his land. His statement: (The land of the Arabs and what its inhabitants accepted Islam or was conquered by force and divided among the spoils is tithe land). As for the land of the Arabs, because the Prophet (ﷺ) and the Rightly Guided Caliphs (may Allah be pleased with them all) did not take land tax from the land of the Arabs. It was criticized in al-Bināyah that this has no basis in hadith books, and he did not respond to it. The response is that absence does not require a basis, because if they had taken land tax from them, it would have been transmitted, and since it is not transmitted, it indicates its absence. And because it is like war booty, so it is not established on their lands just as it is not established on their persons. This is because the condition for imposing land tax is that the inhabitants remain upon disbelief, as in the Sawād of Iraq, and the polytheists of the Arabs are only accepted with Islam or the sword. It is mentioned in al-Maghrib with attribution to the Book of Tithe and Land Tax: Abu Yusuf in al-Amālī: The boundaries of the land of the Arabs are what lies beyond the boundaries of the land of Kufa to the farthest rock in Yemen. And from Muhammad: from ʻAdan Abyan to Syria and what borders it. In Sharḥ al-Qudūrī, al-Karkhī said: It is the land of Hijaz, Tihamah, Yemen, Mecca, al-Ṭāʼif, and al-Bariyyah meaning the desert. He said: And Muhammad said: The land of the Arabs is from al-ʻUdhayb to Mecca and ʻAdan Abyan to the farthest stone in Yemen in Mahrah. These statements I have not found in language books, and it is clear that whoever narrated 'to the farthest stone (ḥajar)' with sukun and interpreted it as 'side' has altered it because the word 'rock (ṣakhr)' occurs in its place, and it seems they mentioned it as an emphasis on the limit, otherwise he could dispense with it. End from al-Maghrib. And 'Jazirat al-ʻArab' means its land and its settlement. In al-Bināyah: al-ʻUdhayb - with ḍammah on the ʻayn and fatḥah on the dhāl and muʻjamah and with bāʼ mawḥḥidah - is a water source for Tamīm. And al-Ḥajar - with two fatḥahs - meaning rock, and Mahrah - with fatḥah on the haa and sukun - is the name of a man, and it is said...
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It opens the chapter on tithe, land tax, and jizya. The author (Zaylaʻi) first defines the terms: al-ʻushr (tithe) is singular of 'usharah, and al-kharāj is the produce extracted from land or even a boy, but here it refers to what the ruler collects from land. The matn statement from Kanz al-Daqāʼiq declares: 'The land of the Arabs, and whatever land whose inhabitants accepted Islam, or was conquered by force and divided among the spoils, is tithe land (ʻushriyyah).' The commentary explains that Arab lands are tithe lands because the Prophet and the caliphs never took kharāj from them. A criticism from al-Bināyah that this has no hadith basis is answered by saying that absence of evidence is evidence of absence – if kharāj had been taken, it would have been reported. Moreover, kharāj is only justified when the inhabitants remain kuffār, but Arab polytheists had no option but Islam or death, so kharāj cannot be imposed on them. The passage then provides geographical definitions of Arab lands from various authorities: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Karkhī, and others, with locations like al-ʻUdhayb, ʻAdan Abyan, etc. The commentary notes these definitions are not found in standard language books.

Key Terms
العشر (al-ʻushr): Tithe, a 10% levy on agricultural produce from land classified as ʻushriyyah.
الخراج (al-kharāj): Land tax imposed on kharājī lands, typically a fixed annual amount or a share of produce, taken from non-Muslim inhabitants or owners.
العنوة (al-ʻanwah): Conquest by force, as opposed to ṣulḥ (treaty).
العذيب (al-ʻUdhayb): A water source for the Tamim tribe, used as a boundary marker for Arab lands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Karkhi's definition, which of the following is NOT part of Arab lands?
A) Hijaz
B) Sawād of Iraq
C) Yemen
D) Tihamah

Key Takeaway
Hanafi jurists defined Arab lands with specific geographical markers, ensuring that all regions within those boundaries are classified as ʻushri and subject to tithe.

Kharāj Land: Sawād and Conquered Territories
Ruling with proof: classification of kharāj lands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the criteria for a land to be classified as kharājīyah and explain the evidence from the practice of ʻUmar.

Core Idea
Land in Sawād and lands conquered by force or treaty with non-Muslim inhabitants are kharājī — the tax is on the land.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʼiq establishes a foundational rule in Hanafi land tax law: the Sawād of Iraq and lands taken by force or treaty where the original inhabitants remain are classified as kharāj lands. The ruling is rooted in the consensus (ijmāʿ) of the Companions under Caliph ʻUmar. Understanding this classification is essential for distinguishing between ʿushrī and kharājī lands, which affects tax obligations even when ownership changes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of land
Note the three categories: Sawād (the cultivated lands of Iraq), lands conquered by force (ʿanwatan) with inhabitants left, and lands conquered by treaty (ṣulḥan) with inhabitants left.
The classification hinges on whether the original non-Muslim inhabitants remain on the land.
2
State the ruling for each
All three are kharājīyah: the land tax (kharāj) is imposed on the land itself, regardless of who owns it.
Kharāj is a perpetual obligation on the land, not on the owner's faith.
3
Understand the proof
The Prophet's companion ʻUmar imposed kharāj on the Sawād with the presence and tacit approval of the other Companions, establishing a binding precedent (ijmāʿ).
This is a dalīl naqlī with qaṭʿī thubūt and dalālah.
4
Recognize the scope
The text provides geographical boundaries for the Sawād of Kufa and Basra, showing precise application.
But the principle extends to any land meeting the criteria, not just these regions.
5
Apply the consequences
When land is kharājī, it remains so even if transferred to a Muslim. The tax is on the land, not the owner.
This impacts zakah and other financial obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما فتح عنوة وأقر أهله عليه أو فتح صلحاً خراجية ولو أحيا أرضاً مواتا يعتبر قربه
قوله : (والسواد وما فتح عنوة وأقر أهله عليه أو فتح صلحاً خراجية) أما السواد فالمراد به سواد العراق فلأن عمر رضي الله عنه وضع عليه الخراج بمحضر من الصحابة ينقل فيه أثر معين وفي البناية: المراد بالسواد القرى وبه صرح التمرتاشي. وسمي السواد الخضرة أشجاره وزورعه وقال الأترازي : المراد من السواد المذكور سواد الكوفة وهو سواد العراق وحده من العذيب إلى عقبة حلوان عرضا العلث إلى عبادان طولاً، وأما سواد البصرة فالأهواز وفارس اهـ. وتقدم ضبط العذيب. وحلوان - بضم الحاء - اسم بلد والعَلْث - بفتح العين المهملة وسكون اللام وبالثاء المثلثة - قرية موقوفة على العلوية على شرقي دجلة وهو أول العراق. وعبادان - بتشديد الباء الموحدة - حصن صغير على شط البحر وفي المثل ما وراء عبادان قرية. وفي شرح الوجيز : طول سواد العراق مائة وستون فرسخاً، وعرضه ثمانون فرسخاً، ومساحته ستة وثلاثون ألف ألف جريب؛ كذا في البناية وأما ما أقر أهلها عليها سواء فتحت قهراً أو صلحاً فلأن الحاجة إلى ابتداء التوظيف على الكافر والخراج أليق به، ويلحق بما أقر أهله عليها ما نقل إليها غير أهلها من الكفار فإنها خراجية كما ذكره الأسبيجابي.
And what was conquered by force and its inhabitants were left upon it, or conquered by treaty, is kharāj land, even if someone revives dead land, its proximity is considered.
His statement: (And al-Sawād, and what was conquered by force and its inhabitants were left upon it, or conquered by treaty, is kharāj land). As for al-Sawād, what is meant is the Sawād of Iraq, because ʻUmar (may Allah be pleased with him) imposed kharāj upon it in the presence of the Companions, transmitting a specific narration. In al-Bināyah: What is meant by al-Sawād is the villages; al-Tamartāshī explicitly stated this. It was named al-Sawād due to the greenness of its trees and crops. Al-Atrazī said: What is meant by the mentioned al-Sawād is the Sawād of Kufa, which is the Sawād of Iraq. Its boundary is from al-ʻUdhayb to ʻUqbah Ḥulwān widthwise, and from al-ʻAlth to ʻAbbādān lengthwise. As for the Sawād of Basra, it is al-Ahwāz and Fārs. End. The spelling of al-ʻUdhayb was given earlier. Ḥulwān - with ḍammah on the ḥāʼ - is a name of a town. Al-ʻAlth - with fatḥah on the ʻayn, sukun on the lām, and thāʼ muthallathah - is a village endowed to the ʻAlawids on the east bank of the Tigris, and it is the beginning of Iraq. ʻAbbādān - with tashdīd on the bāʼ - is a small fortress on the seashore, and the proverb says: 'Beyond ʻAbbādān there is no village.' In Sharḥ al-Wajīz: The length of Sawād Iraq is one hundred sixty farsakhs, and its width is eighty farsakhs, and its area is thirty-six thousand thousand jarībs. So in al-Bināyah. As for what its inhabitants were left upon, whether conquered by force or treaty, because the need for initial taxation is upon the disbeliever, and kharāj is more suitable for them. And attached to what its inhabitants were left upon is what non-native disbelievers are transferred to it, for it is kharāj land, as mentioned by al-Asbījābī.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn states that al-Sawād (the Sawād of Iraq) and lands conquered by force where the inhabitants were allowed to stay, or lands conquered by treaty, are kharāj lands (kharājiyyah). The commentary explains that Sawād refers to the Sawād of Iraq, where Caliph ʻUmar imposed kharāj with the consensus of the Companions. The geographical boundaries are given: from al-ʻUdhayb to ʻUqbah Ḥulwān in width, and from al-ʻAlth to ʻAbbādān in length. For Sawād of Basra, it is al-Ahwāz and Fārs. The reason for kharāj is that the inhabitants are non-Muslims, and kharāj is more appropriate for them. Even if land is transferred to other disbelievers, it remains kharāj. This classification is based on the need to impose a tax on the kāfir, and kharāj suits that purpose.

Key Terms
السواد (al-Sawād): The cultivated lands of Iraq, specifically the Sawād of Kufa and Basra, upon which ʻUmar imposed kharāj.
خراجية (kharājiyyah): Land subject to kharāj (land tax) regardless of who owns it; the tax is a perpetual obligation on the land itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Caliph ʻUmar impose kharāj on the Sawād of Iraq?
A) Because the land was conquered by treaty.
B) Because the inhabitants were Muslims.
C) Because the inhabitants remained non-Muslims and the Sahābah agreed to impose kharāj.
D) Because he wanted to encourage cultivation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies Sawād and lands conquered by force or treaty with non-Muslim inhabitants as kharājī lands, based on the consensus of the Companions.
